Refuting the Claim that Kufr is Ugly in Itself
The author refutes the claim that kufr is ugly in itself and shows its absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical refutation of the Mu'tazili claim that kufr is ugly in itself, and see how it leads to a fatal contradiction.

Core Idea
If kufr is ugly by nature, God's will is implicated; denying that leads to absurdity.

The Mu'tazilites argued that acts like kufr are inherently ugly, independent of divine command. In this passage, the author turns their own logic against them, exposing a dilemma: either God willed that ugliness, or He did not. Both options lead to conclusions the Mu'tazilites cannot accept, ultimately forcing them into the absurd position of having to call kufr 'good'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure of the argument: it presents two options and then draws a conclusion.
The passage is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The author presents two possibilities regarding the Mu'tazili claim. First, if God made kufr ugly, then He must have willed its essence. Second, if they say God did not will it to be ugly, then what follows? Find both in the passage.
The first horn is implied by 'إذا الله قبحه فقد أراد عينه'.
3
Understand the consequence of the second horn
If the opponents say God does not will kufr to be ugly, then according to their own taxonomy, whatever is not ugly is good. This leads to the conclusion that kufr is good, which they cannot accept.
This is the key turning point: the opponent's own principle is used against them.
4
Recognize the final absurdity
The author concludes that claiming kufr is good is itself kufr. This is a rhetorical and theological knockout: the Mu'tazili position, if followed consistently, leads to a self-refuting statement.
This shows the danger of building an ethical system independent of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: نعم - وهو قولهم - قيل : والكفر قبيح لعينه فإذا الله قبحه فقد أراد عينه إذ وهذا ما أنكرتموه ، وإن قالوا لا يريد أن يكون قبيحًا ، فقد أراد أن يكون من مذهبهم أن ما ليس بقبيح فهو حسن ولهذا زعموا أن كل مباح حسن، وزعموا أن الوجوب أو الندب يقتضي حسنًا زائدًا على أصل الحسن، والقول بأن الكفر حسن كفر صريح
They said: Yes – and that is their statement – it is said: And kufr is ugly in itself. So if God made it ugly, then He willed its very essence, and this is what you denied. And if they say: He does not will that it be ugly, then He willed that it be from their doctrine that whatever is not ugly is good. Hence they claim that every permissible thing is good, and they claim that obligation or recommendation entails an additional goodness beyond the original goodness. And the statement that kufr is good is explicit kufr.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of the Mu'tazili claim that kufr is ugly in itself. The author begins by quoting the opponent's statement that kufr is ugly in itself. He then points out an inconsistency: if God made kufr ugly, then God must have willed its essence (since making something ugly is an act of will), but the opponents deny that God wills kufr. If, on the other hand, they say that God does not will kufr to be ugly, then according to their own principle, whatever is not ugly is good. Thus, kufr would be considered good, which leads to the absurd conclusion that claiming kufr is good is itself kufr. The author thus exposes a logical flaw in their position.

Key Terms
كفر
قبيح
حسن
إرادة
مذهب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the author is endorsing the view that kufr is actually good.
Correction: The author is not claiming kufr is good; he is showing that the Mu'tazili premise forces them to that absurd conclusion, which is itself kufr.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue would happen if the opponents say God does not will kufr to be ugly?
A) Kufr would become permissible.
B) Kufr would be good according to their own doctrine.
C) It would disprove God's omnipotence.
D) It would make kufr forbidden.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili claim that kufr is inherently ugly leads to a dilemma: either God willed kufr, or kufr becomes good—both of which they must reject, making their position incoherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If someone were to argue that disbelief is obviously evil and God cannot possibly will it, how would you respond using the logic of this passage? What does that reveal about your own reliance on reason versus revelation?
?
The Mu'tazilites claimed to defend God's justice, but their reasoning led to kufr. Where in your own thinking might you be overconfident in your intellect, assuming you can judge what God must do? Will you submit your judgments to the Qur'an and Sunnah even when they seem uncomfortable?

Refuting the Compulsion Argument from Divine Will and Knowledge
The author responds to the objection that divine will and knowledge necessitate compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that divine will and knowledge compel human actions, preserving human free will.

Core Idea
God's will and knowledge encompass free choices, not coercion.

A common objection against free will is that if God wills and knows everything, humans have no real choice. The author tackles this head-on, showing that God's attributes do not negate human agency. This passage presents two clear arguments and a powerful parallel to demonstrate that divine will and knowledge are compatible with human freedom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and the literal translation to get the gist before diving into analysis.
Pay attention to the structure: two objections followed by refutations.
2
Identify the first argument: God's will
Notice how the author responds to the objection about God's will. He says God wills the voluntary act, not the forced one.
This is key: the object of God's will is the free act, so the act remains voluntary.
3
Identify the second argument: God's knowledge
Follow the logical dilemma the author presents: if the opponent says the slave cannot escape God's knowledge, then either he affirms compulsion (invalidating his doctrine) or denies it (eliminating the objection).
This is a clever refutation using the opponent's own premises.
4
Understand the parallel with God's actions
See how the author uses God's own voluntary actions as an analogy: God knows what He does but is not compelled, so similarly the slave is not compelled.
This reinforces the consistency of the argument.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Consider how this passage corrects the misconception that divine foreknowledge or will necessitate compulsion.
The key is that God's knowledge and will encompass free acts without negating their freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يقولون : إن العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عن إرادة الله تعالى فيصير مجبوراً.
قلنا : ونعلم يقينًا أنه ليس بمجبور ، وهذا لأنه يريد أن يوجد فعله الاختياري لا الاضطراري فيخرج اختياريًا لا اضطراريًا كما أراد.
ثم يقال : والعبد لا يمكنه الخروج عن علم الله تعالى فيكون مجبوراً فإن قال: نعم. أبطل مذهبه وارتكب محالاً، وإن قال : لا ، أبطل شبهته، وكذا الله تعالى لا يخرج عن معلومه وليس بمضطر لما علم أنه يفعل ما يفعل باختياره فلم يكن هوا مضطرًا ولا العبد ، فكذا إذا أراد أن العبد يفعل ما يفعل باختياره لم يصر مضطرًا
والله الموفق.
And they say: The slave cannot exit from the will of God, so he becomes compelled. We say: And we know with certainty that he is not compelled. This is because He wills that he should bring about his voluntary act, not the forced one, so he does it voluntarily, not forced, as He willed. Then it is said: And the slave cannot exit from the knowledge of God, so he becomes compelled. So if he says: Yes, he invalidates his doctrine and commits an impossibility. If he says: No, he invalidates his objection. Likewise, God does not exit from His known and is not constrained because He knows that He does what He does by His choice. So He is not constrained, nor is the slave. Similarly, when He wills that the slave does what he does by his choice, he does not become constrained. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that if everything is under God's will and knowledge, then human actions are compelled. The author first responds to the will objection: God wills the voluntary act, not the forced one, so the act is freely chosen. Then he addresses the knowledge objection: if the opponent says that the slave cannot escape God's knowledge and is therefore compelled, then either he affirms compulsion (which invalidates his doctrine) or he denies it (which invalidates his objection). The author then uses a parallel argument for God: God knows His own actions are voluntary, so He is not compelled, and the same applies to the slave. Therefore, the objection is refuted.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's absolute will and comprehensive knowledge leave no room for human free will; every action is compelled by God.
Correction: The author shows that God's will and knowledge are compatible with human free will because God wills and knows the voluntary choices of humans without coercing them. The parallel with God's own voluntary acts illustrates that knowledge does not imply compulsion.

Checkpoint

A) It proves compulsion.
B) It invalidates his own doctrine.
C) It shows God's power.
D) It proves the slave is free.

Key Takeaway
Divine will and knowledge encompass human free choices without compelling them, as shown by the fact that God wills only voluntary acts and His own knowledge does not compel His voluntary actions.

The Reality of Allah's Decree: Qada' and Maqdi
Defines qada' as right and true, explains kufr is decreed but not itself qada'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction between Allah's decree (qada') and that which is decreed (maqdi), and how a believer should relate to both.

Core Idea
Allah's decree is always right; it is the decreed thing that may be evil.

This lesson addresses a subtle but crucial point in Islamic theology: how can we affirm that Allah's decree is entirely good and wise when we see that He decrees disbelief and sin? The passage from Imam al-Nasafi clarifies that we must distinguish between the act of decreeing (qada'), which is always true and wise, and the thing decreed (maqdi), which may be false and evil. Our attitude toward each differs accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the distinction between qada' and maqdi that the author introduces.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Understand the key distinction
Identify where the author says 'kufr is maqdi, not qada'. Understand that qada' is the act of decreeing, while maqdi is the object decreed.
This distinction is central to the Maturidi position.
3
Grasp the wisdom in decreeing evil
The author says qada' of evil is correct because of the wisdom in it. Reflect on how Allah's decree always has a wise purpose, even if we do not see it.
This relates to the creation of actions (khalq al-af'al).
4
Apply the correct attitude
The passage concludes with the believer's attitude: pleased with qada' but not with the attribute of kufr in oneself. Understand why this is balanced.
This guards against fatalism and rejecting divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقضاء الله تعالى حق وصواب وبه احتج الكعبي. وعندنا أن الكفر مقضي الله تعالى لا قضاؤه، وقضاؤه حق وصواب، ومقضيه باطل، وقضاء هذا المقضي صواب، لما فيه من الحكمة على ما بينا في مسألة خلق الأفعال، فمن رضي يجعل الله تعالى الكفر باطلاً قبيحًا شرًا فقد رضى بقضاء الله تعالى، ومن لم يرض بذلك فهو غير راض بقضاء الله، ومن رضي بذلك ولم يرض أن يكون الكفر صفة له ولم يحب أن يفعله في نفسه فقد رضي بقضاء الله تعالى ولم يرضى بما يوجب مقته وتعذيبه.
And the decree (qada') of Allah the Exalted is true and correct. By it, al-Ka'bi argued. According to us, disbelief (kufr) is that which is decreed (maqdi) by Allah, not His decree (qada'). His decree is true and correct, while what is decreed is false. And the decreeing (qada') of this decreed thing is correct, because of the wisdom in it, as we explained in the issue of the creation of actions. So whoever is pleased that Allah the Exalted makes disbelief false, ugly, and evil, then he is pleased with the decree of Allah the Exalted. And whoever is not pleased with that, then he is not pleased with the decree of Allah. And whoever is pleased with that but is not pleased that disbelief be a description for him and does not love to perform it in himself, then he is pleased with the decree of Allah the Exalted and is not pleased with what necessitates His wrath and punishment.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of qada' (divine decree) in relation to disbelief. It begins by stating that the decree of Allah is true and correct (haqq wa sawab), and mentions that al-Ka'bi (a Mu'tazili scholar) used this premise to argue against the Ahl al-Sunna. Then it clarifies the position of the Maturidis: disbelief (kufr) is something decreed by Allah (maqdi), not itself His decree (qada'). The act of decreeing is always right because of the wisdom behind it, even if the decreed thing (al-maqdi) is itself false and evil. This wisdom is elaborated in the issue of the creation of actions. The passage then explains the correct attitude: a believer should be pleased with Allah's decree because it entails wisdom, but he should not be pleased with the attribute of disbelief for himself or desire to commit it. Thus, one can be pleased with the decree without being pleased with the decreed thing that brings punishment. This guards against two errors: (1) rejecting divine decree because of the evilness of what is decreed, and (2) approving of evil because it is decreed.

Key Terms
قضاء
مقضي
حق وصواب
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That being pleased with qada' requires being pleased with the content of what is decreed, even if it is sin or disbelief.
Correction: One can be pleased with the decree (qada') without being pleased with the decreed thing (maqdi) that is evil, because the decree has wisdom while the decreed thing may be blameworthy.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the correct attitude towards Allah's decree when it includes disbelief?
A) One must be displeased with the decree because it contains evil.
B) One must be pleased with the decree for its wisdom, but not pleased with disbelief as a personal attribute.
C) One must be equally pleased with both the decree and the decreed disbelief.
D) One must reject the decree because it is not compatible with Allah's justice.

Key Takeaway
Allah's decree is always true and wise; we must be content with it, but we are not required to be content with the evil decreed as part of our own actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own sins and failures, do you secretly resent Allah for decreeing them? Can you truly say, 'I am pleased with Your decree, but I hate that this sin became my action'? Where does your heart stand between these two?
?
Is there a trial in your life that you have struggled to accept, believing it is unjust? How does the distinction between qada' and maqdi change your perspective on that trial? Will you now surrender to His decree while still striving against the evil within it?
?
You claim to be pleased with Allah's decree. But are you also pleased when He decrees something good for someone you dislike? Examine your heart: does your pleasure depend on who benefits? If so, you have not truly understood this lesson. Repent and realign your heart today.

The Maturidi View and the Mu'tazila Denial of Divine Creation of Acts
Maturidi and Mu'tazila foundational statements on guidance and misguidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational disagreement between the Maturidis and Mu'tazila regarding whether Allah creates the acts of guidance and misguidance in servants.

Core Idea
Allah creates all acts, even guidance and misguidance; the Mu'tazila reject this.

The author begins this section by stating the Maturidi position on divine guidance and misguidance. He then contrasts it with the Mu'tazila's fundamental denial that Allah can create human actions. This short passage sets the stage for the detailed Mu'tazila reinterpretations that follow. Let's read the two opposing views directly.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first few lines of the source passage in Arabic. Note the direct statement of the Maturidi view and the Mu'tazila's contrary position.
Pay attention to the contrast between 'وجد منه الهدى والإضلال' and 'لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال'.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on the words هدى, إضلال, خلق أفعال العباد. Understand how they are used to express the disagreement.
3
Compare the two positions
Notice that the Maturidi conclusion is based on the premise that Allah creates all acts, while the Mu'tazila start from the denial of that premise. Ask yourself: what does each school affirm about divine agency?
This disagreement is the root of all subsequent discussions on guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الهدى والإضلال
لما ثبت أن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد فكان هو الذي خلق فيهم فعل الاهتداء وفعل الضلال، فوجد منه الهدى والإضلال.
وعند المعتزلة لما لم يجز أن يخلق أفعالهم لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال، ويقولون ما أضيف إلى الله تعالى من الهداية فالمراد منه بيان طريق الدين لا تخليق فعل الاهتداء، وما أضيف إليه من الإزاغة والإضلال والخذلان والطبع بقوله: (وَطَبَعَ اللهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ) والمد بقوله: ﴿وَيَمُدُّهُمْ فِي طُغْيَانِهِمْ يَعْمَهُونَ) فلأن السبب الذي كان به منهم الأفعال كان من الله تعالى كالقدر والآلات، وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى مسببها، وكذا في الهداية والعصمة قد تضاف على هذا الطريق، وقد يقولون بأنها تضاف إليه على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى شروطها التي توجد هي عندها إذ لولا المحنة والتكليف لما وجدت منهم هذه المعاني وإنما وجدت عند التكليف فتضاف إليه، وإن لم يكن منه فيها فعل كما يضاف إلى القرآن: فَزَادَهُمْ إِيمَنَا) فَزَادَتْهُمْ رِجْسًا وإلى الدعاء أنه: (وَزَادَهُمْ) تفورا: وإلى الأصنام: إِنَّهُنَّ أَضْلَلْنَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ النَّاسِ وقد يقولون: إنها تضاف إليه لأنها حملت عقيب أحوال أوجدها الله تعالى تصير تلك الأحوال حاملة لهم عليها من نحو الإنعام والإمهال مع علمهم بقدرته، والتقرر عندهم أن من عصى من له القدرة عليه لا يمهله بل يعالجه بالتعذيب والتنكيل، ثم الله تعالى لم يعاقبهم بل أمهلهم، ولم يكتف بالإمهال حتى أدر عليهم سوابغ نعمه وتركهم يتقلبون في آثار أفضاله ويترددون في أثناء منته وإنعامه، فظنوا أن ذلك لرضا الله تعالى بصنيعهم واستحسانه ما هم عليه من النحل والمذاهب حتى ادعوا الأمر فقالوا والله أمرنا بها، فصار ذلك مبعثةً لهم على التمسك بما هم عليه فأضيف إليه كما يضاف إلى الدنيا الغرور لاغترار الناس بها لما هي عليه من حالة الزهرة والبهجة، وربما يقولون ما يضاف إليه من الهداية فالمراد منه هداية المحسنين طريق الجنة في الآخرة، وهذا التأويل محكي عن الجبائي، ويقولون في معنى الإضلال المضاف إلى الله تعالى: إنه ليس بتخليق فعل الضلال بل هو تسميته إياه ضالاً يقال: أضله أي سماه أي سماه ضالاً.
قال الكميت:
فطائفة قد أكفروني بحبكم وطائفة قالوا مسيء ومذنب
Discussion on guidance and misguidance. Since it is established that Allah the Exalted created the actions of servants, He is the one who created in them the act of guidance and the act of misguidance, so guidance and misguidance are from Him. According to the Mu'tazila, since it is not permissible that He creates their actions, no creation of the act of guidance nor creation of the act of misguidance is from Him. They say that what is attributed to Allah the Exalted of guidance means the explanation of the path of religion, not the creation of the act of guidance. And what is attributed to Him of causing deviation, misguidance, abandonment, and sealing, by His saying: (And Allah has set a seal upon their hearts) and prolonging by His saying: (And He prolongs them in their transgression, wandering blindly), it is because the cause by which actions occur from them was from Allah the Exalted, like power and instruments, and actions are sometimes attributed to their cause. Similarly, guidance and protection (isma) are attributed in this way. And they sometimes say that they are attributed to Him according to the attribution of things to their conditions, which exist when they occur, for if not for trial and obligation, these meanings would not have occurred from them; they occur only at obligation, so they are attributed to Him, even though no act from Him is in them, just as it is attributed to the Qur'an: (So it increased them in faith) and increased them in abomination, and to supplication that it increased them in aversion, and to idols: (They have led many people astray). And they sometimes say that they are attributed to Him because they occur after states that Allah the Exalted brought about, making those states cause them to adhere, such as beneficence and respite along with their knowledge of His power, and their conviction that whoever disobeys the One who has power over him does not give him respite but rather punishes and torments him. Then Allah the Exalted did not punish them but gave them respite, and not content with respite, He poured upon them abundant favours and left them turning in the traces of His bounty and wandering amidst His boons and beneficence. So they thought that was due to Allah's pleasure with their deeds and His approval of their sects and doctrines, until they claimed the matter and said: God commanded us with it. So that became an incentive for them to cling to what they were upon, so it was attributed to Him, just as the world is attributed to deception because people are deceived by it due to its state of bloom and beauty. And they sometimes say that what is attributed to Him of guidance means the guidance of the righteous to the path of Paradise in the Hereafter. This interpretation is reported from al-Jubba'i. And they say concerning the meaning of misguidance attributed to Allah the Exalted: It is not the creation of the act of misguidance, but rather it is His naming him 'misguided'. It is said: 'adalla' meaning he named him, i.e., he named him misguided. Al-Kumayt said: A group has declared me disbeliever for loving you, and a group said: sinful and guilty.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi position on divine guidance and misguidance, followed by an extensive exposition of the Mu'tazila interpretation. The author begins by stating the Maturidi premise: since Allah creates all actions of servants, He creates in them both the act of guidance (ihtida') and the act of misguidance (dalaal), thus guidance and misguidance originate from Him. The passage then shifts to the Mu'tazila view, who deny that Allah creates human actions. They reinterpret all scriptural attributions of guidance and misguidance to Allah. Specifically: 1) Guidance (huda) attributed to Allah means the explanation of the religious path (bayan tariq al-din), not the creation of the act of guidance. 2) Attributions of misguidance (idlaal), causing deviation (izaagha), abandonment (khidhlaan), sealing (tab'), and prolonging (madd) are explained by causality: Allah creates the causes (like power and organs) through which actions occur, and actions are sometimes attributed to their causes. Similarly, guidance and protection (isma) are attributed to Allah as causes. 3) Another Mu'tazila explanation: these attributes are conditional – if not for Allah's trial and obligation, those states would not have arisen; they arise at obligation, so they are attributed to Allah, though He performs no act in them. Analogies are given: the Qur'an increases faith or abomination, supplication increases aversion, idols lead astray – all are attributed to secondary causes. 4) A further explanation: Allah creates states (like beneficence and respite) that, combined with people's knowledge that disobedience warrants immediate punishment, lead them to think their well-being indicates divine approval, thus they persist in error. This is likened to the worldly life being called deceptive. 5) Regarding guidance, some Mu'tazila say it refers to the guidance of the righteous to Paradise in the Hereafter, an interpretation from al-Jubba'i. 6) Regarding misguidance (idlaal), it means simply naming someone 'misguided', not creating the act. A poet's verse is cited where 'adalla' means called him misguided. Thus the Mu'tazila systematically reinterpret all apparent divine causation of human misguidance.

Key Terms
هدى
إضلال
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view in this passage, why are guidance and misguidance from Allah?
A) Because Allah commands guidance and forbids misguidance.
B) Because Allah creates all actions of servants, including the acts of guidance and misguidance.
C) Because Allah decrees guidance and misguidance for each person.
D) Because Allah knows who will be guided or misguided.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi and Mu'tazila diverge on whether Allah creates human actions, which directly shapes their understanding of divine guidance and misguidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that Allah created the very act of guidance in your heart, does your gratitude for every moment of faith deepen? How does this truth move you to thank Him not just in words but in action today?
?
If Allah had not created the act of misguidance in some people, as the Mu'tazila claim, then who would be responsible for their disbelief? Does this make you more aware of your absolute dependence on Allah's mercy to keep you on the straight path? What will you do to hold onto that mercy?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected this teaching because they thought it made Allah unjust. But do you sometimes judge Allah's actions by your own sense of justice? How does this passage challenge you to submit to His sovereignty even where you do not fully understand?

Mu'tazila Reinterpretations of Divine Guidance and Misguidance
Mu'tazila detailed reinterpretations of divine guidance and misguidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various ways the Mu'tazila reinterpret scriptural attributions of guidance and misguidance to Allah, avoiding direct creation of human acts.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila explain divine guidance and misguidance as causal, conditional, or linguistic, not as creation of acts.

After denying that Allah creates the acts of guidance and misguidance, the Mu'tazila must reinterpret the many Quranic verses that attribute guidance and misguidance to Allah. This passage presents several of their explanations: from guidance as mere explanation of the path, to attributing misguidance to Allah as the cause of conditions, to a linguistic interpretation of 'naming' someone misguided. These subtle arguments show how the Mu'tazila maintain divine involvement without compromising human free will.

Guided Path
1
List the different explanations
Read the passage and identify each distinct Mu'tazila explanation for the divine attribution of guidance and misguidance. There are at least four main ones.
Look for phrases like 'يقولون', 'قد يقولون'.
2
Understand the causal explanation
The first explanation: guidance and misguidance are attributed to Allah as causes (like power and instruments). Note the example of attributing actions to their causes.
3
Examine the conditional explanation
The second explanation: they are attributed as conditions (shurut) that are necessary for the actions to occur, like trial and obligation.
Contrast with direct creation.
4
Consider the state-based and naming explanations
The third explanation: Allah creates states that lead people to persist, and the fourth: 'idlaal' means simply naming someone misguided. See the poet's evidence.
These show the creativity of Mu'tazila hermeneutics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الهدى والإضلال
لما ثبت أن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد فكان هو الذي خلق فيهم فعل الاهتداء وفعل الضلال، فوجد منه الهدى والإضلال.
وعند المعتزلة لما لم يجز أن يخلق أفعالهم لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال، ويقولون ما أضيف إلى الله تعالى من الهداية فالمراد منه بيان طريق الدين لا تخليق فعل الاهتداء، وما أضيف إليه من الإزاغة والإضلال والخذلان والطبع بقوله: (وَطَبَعَ اللهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ) والمد بقوله: ﴿وَيَمُدُّهُمْ فِي طُغْيَانِهِمْ يَعْمَهُونَ) فلأن السبب الذي كان به منهم الأفعال كان من الله تعالى كالقدر والآلات، وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى مسببها، وكذا في الهداية والعصمة قد تضاف على هذا الطريق، وقد يقولون بأنها تضاف إليه على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى شروطها التي توجد هي عندها إذ لولا المحنة والتكليف لما وجدت منهم هذه المعاني وإنما وجدت عند التكليف فتضاف إليه، وإن لم يكن منه فيها فعل كما يضاف إلى القرآن: فَزَادَهُمْ إِيمَنَا) فَزَادَتْهُمْ رِجْسًا وإلى الدعاء أنه: (وَزَادَهُمْ) تفورا: وإلى الأصنام: إِنَّهُنَّ أَضْلَلْنَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ النَّاسِ وقد يقولون: إنها تضاف إليه لأنها حملت عقيب أحوال أوجدها الله تعالى تصير تلك الأحوال حاملة لهم عليها من نحو الإنعام والإمهال مع علمهم بقدرته، والتقرر عندهم أن من عصى من له القدرة عليه لا يمهله بل يعالجه بالتعذيب والتنكيل، ثم الله تعالى لم يعاقبهم بل أمهلهم، ولم يكتف بالإمهال حتى أدر عليهم سوابغ نعمه وتركهم يتقلبون في آثار أفضاله ويترددون في أثناء منته وإنعامه، فظنوا أن ذلك لرضا الله تعالى بصنيعهم واستحسانه ما هم عليه من النحل والمذاهب حتى ادعوا الأمر فقالوا والله أمرنا بها، فصار ذلك مبعثةً لهم على التمسك بما هم عليه فأضيف إليه كما يضاف إلى الدنيا الغرور لاغترار الناس بها لما هي عليه من حالة الزهرة والبهجة، وربما يقولون ما يضاف إليه من الهداية فالمراد منه هداية المحسنين طريق الجنة في الآخرة، وهذا التأويل محكي عن الجبائي، ويقولون في معنى الإضلال المضاف إلى الله تعالى: إنه ليس بتخليق فعل الضلال بل هو تسميته إياه ضالاً يقال: أضله أي سماه أي سماه ضالاً.
قال الكميت:
فطائفة قد أكفروني بحبكم وطائفة قالوا مسيء ومذنب
Discussion on guidance and misguidance. Since it is established that Allah the Exalted created the actions of servants, He is the one who created in them the act of guidance and the act of misguidance, so guidance and misguidance are from Him. According to the Mu'tazila, since it is not permissible that He creates their actions, no creation of the act of guidance nor creation of the act of misguidance is from Him. They say that what is attributed to Allah the Exalted of guidance means the explanation of the path of religion, not the creation of the act of guidance. And what is attributed to Him of causing deviation, misguidance, abandonment, and sealing, by His saying: (And Allah has set a seal upon their hearts) and prolonging by His saying: (And He prolongs them in their transgression, wandering blindly), it is because the cause by which actions occur from them was from Allah the Exalted, like power and instruments, and actions are sometimes attributed to their cause. Similarly, guidance and protection (isma) are attributed in this way. And they sometimes say that they are attributed to Him according to the attribution of things to their conditions, which exist when they occur, for if not for trial and obligation, these meanings would not have occurred from them; they occur only at obligation, so they are attributed to Him, even though no act from Him is in them, just as it is attributed to the Qur'an: (So it increased them in faith) and increased them in abomination, and to supplication that it increased them in aversion, and to idols: (They have led many people astray). And they sometimes say that they are attributed to Him because they occur after states that Allah the Exalted brought about, making those states cause them to adhere, such as beneficence and respite along with their knowledge of His power, and their conviction that whoever disobeys the One who has power over him does not give him respite but rather punishes and torments him. Then Allah the Exalted did not punish them but gave them respite, and not content with respite, He poured upon them abundant favours and left them turning in the traces of His bounty and wandering amidst His boons and beneficence. So they thought that was due to Allah's pleasure with their deeds and His approval of their sects and doctrines, until they claimed the matter and said: God commanded us with it. So that became an incentive for them to cling to what they were upon, so it was attributed to Him, just as the world is attributed to deception because people are deceived by it due to its state of bloom and beauty. And they sometimes say that what is attributed to Him of guidance means the guidance of the righteous to the path of Paradise in the Hereafter. This interpretation is reported from al-Jubba'i. And they say concerning the meaning of misguidance attributed to Allah the Exalted: It is not the creation of the act of misguidance, but rather it is His naming him 'misguided'. It is said: 'adalla' meaning he named him, i.e., he named him misguided. Al-Kumayt said: A group has declared me disbeliever for loving you, and a group said: sinful and guilty.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi position on divine guidance and misguidance, followed by an extensive exposition of the Mu'tazila interpretation. The author begins by stating the Maturidi premise: since Allah creates all actions of servants, He creates in them both the act of guidance (ihtida') and the act of misguidance (dalaal), thus guidance and misguidance originate from Him. The passage then shifts to the Mu'tazila view, who deny that Allah creates human actions. They reinterpret all scriptural attributions of guidance and misguidance to Allah. Specifically: 1) Guidance (huda) attributed to Allah means the explanation of the religious path (bayan tariq al-din), not the creation of the act of guidance. 2) Attributions of misguidance (idlaal), causing deviation (izaagha), abandonment (khidhlaan), sealing (tab'), and prolonging (madd) are explained by causality: Allah creates the causes (like power and organs) through which actions occur, and actions are sometimes attributed to their causes. Similarly, guidance and protection (isma) are attributed to Allah as causes. 3) Another Mu'tazila explanation: these attributes are conditional – if not for Allah's trial and obligation, those states would not have arisen; they arise at obligation, so they are attributed to Allah, though He performs no act in them. Analogies are given: the Qur'an increases faith or abomination, supplication increases aversion, idols lead astray – all are attributed to secondary causes. 4) A further explanation: Allah creates states (like beneficence and respite) that, combined with people's knowledge that disobedience warrants immediate punishment, lead them to think their well-being indicates divine approval, thus they persist in error. This is likened to the worldly life being called deceptive. 5) Regarding guidance, some Mu'tazila say it refers to the guidance of the righteous to Paradise in the Hereafter, an interpretation from al-Jubba'i. 6) Regarding misguidance (idlaal), it means simply naming someone 'misguided', not creating the act. A poet's verse is cited where 'adalla' means called him misguided. Thus the Mu'tazila systematically reinterpret all apparent divine causation of human misguidance.

Key Terms
بيان طريق الدين
تسمية
سبب
شرط
إضافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila deny any divine involvement in guidance and misguidance.
Correction: The Mu'tazila affirm divine involvement through indirect causation, conditions, and states, as detailed in this passage.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila interpretation in this passage, what does 'idlaal' (إضلال) attributed to Allah mean?
A) Allah creates the act of misguidance in the servant.
B) Allah names the servant 'misguided'.
C) Allah causes the servant to go astray by removing guidance.
D) Allah permits the servant to choose misguidance.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila offer multiple reinterpretations (causal, conditional, state-based, and linguistic) to avoid attributing direct creation of human acts to Allah while still acknowledging His role in guidance and misguidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses that ascribe misguidance to Allah, do you feel a tension between divine control and human responsibility? How does the Mu'tazila's explanation of misguidance as a causal or conditional attribution sit with your heart's need to see Allah as all-powerful yet just? Will you examine your own understanding of these verses more deeply, not just accepting a simple reading?
?
Consider a time you thought someone's blessings meant Allah was pleased with them, only to see them persist in error. How might the Mu'tazila's state-based interpretation — that Allah's favors led them to assume His approval — challenge you to reconsider your own criteria for divine pleasure? Are you willing to humble yourself and ask Allah to guide you through true guidance, not just His outward favors?
?
The Mu'tazila taught that guidance is sometimes just Allah naming someone 'guided' or 'misguided' without creating the act. Do you ever feel that you rely on your own efforts for faith, forgetting that even the desire to seek guidance is from Him? What would it cost you to truly believe that every act of seeking guidance is a gift you do not create? Commit to a specific dua tonight, begging Allah to create guidance in your heart.

Guidance Beyond Clarification: Quranic Proof
Proof from Quranic verses that God's guidance is more than mere clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi school uses Quranic verses to prove that divine guidance involves creating the act of guidance, beyond mere clarification.

Core Idea
God's guidance is not just clarification—it is the creation of faith in the heart.

The Mu'tazilites argued that guidance (hidaya) is nothing more than clarifying the truth (bayan). But the Quran itself shows that guidance must be something more. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents two key verses that demolish the Mu'tazilite interpretation, demonstrating that true guidance comes only from God creating it in the servant.

Guided Path
1
Review the Maturidi premise
The author first reminds us that God creates all actions, including the acts of guidance and misguidance. Keep this in mind as the foundation.
2
Examine the first verse (Q28:56)
Read the verse and the author's reasoning: if guidance were only clarification, the Prophet would guide his loved ones. But he cannot, so guidance must be more.
This is a direct refutation of the Mu'tazilite position.
3
Examine the second verse (Q6:125)
Analyze the verse about expanding and constricting the breast. The author shows that if guidance were mere calling, then every recipient would have an expanded breast, contradicting the verse's division.
This leads to absurdity and disbelief if the Mu'tazilite view is held.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the Mu'tazilite interpretations lead to contradictions and even kufr. The only consistent view is that God creates guidance in whom He wills.
Reflect on how this strengthens the Maturidi position on divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن لما أقمنا الدلالة على أن الله تعالى خالق أفعال العباد كان هاديًا لتخليقه فعل الاهتداء، ومضلاً لتخليقه فعل الضلال. ثم الذي يبطل جميع ما ذهبوا إليه من التأويلات قوله تعالى مخاطبًا لنبيه عليه السلام : إِنَّكَ لَا تَهْدِى مَنْ أَحْبَبْتَ وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِى مَن يَشَاءُ ولو كان الهدى هو البيان لكان النبي عليه السلام يهدي من أحبه ، فدل أن وراء البيان هداية أخرى وليس ذلك إلا ما قلنا يدل على أن الله تعالى قال : ( فَمَن يُرِدِ اللهُ أَن يَهْدِيَهُ يَشْرَحْ صَدْرَهُ لِلْإِسْلَامِ ولو كان المراد من الهداية الدعوة وبيان الطريق ينبغي أن يقال كل من دعاه الله للإيمان وبين له طريق الدين فهو مشروح الصدر، فيصير قوله تعالى: (يَجْعَلْ صَدْرَهُ ضَيِّقًا حَرَجًا باطلاً كذبًا وهو كفر، وكذا كل من يسميه الله تعالى ضالاً ينبغي أن يجعل صدره ضيقًا حرجًا وكذا كل من يجده ضالاً، ثم إن الله تعالى بين الطريق لكل كافر فإذا لم يسلم يجده ضالاً ضالاً ويسميه فينبغي أن يجعل صدره ضيقًا حرجًا، فإذا كل كافر يشرح الله صدره لأنه هداه وضيق صدره لأنه أضله وفيه وصف الله تعالى لفعل ماهو محال، وكذا تقسيم الله تعالى الخلق قسمين: أحدهما شرح صدره، والآخر ضيق صدره باطل وهذا كله كفر.
And we, when we established the proof that God Almighty is the creator of the actions of servants, He is a guide by creating the act of guidance, and a misguider by creating the act of misguidance. Then that which invalidates all the interpretations they have adopted is His saying, addressing His Prophet: 'Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but God guides whom He wills' (Q28:56). And if guidance were merely clarification, then the Prophet would guide whom he loved. So it indicates that behind clarification there is another guidance, and that is not except what we said. It indicates that God Almighty said: 'So whoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast for Islam' (Q6:125). And if the intended meaning of guidance were the call and clarification of the path, it would be necessary to say that everyone whom God calls to faith and clarifies the path of religion for him is of expanded breast. Then His saying: 'He makes his breast tight and constricted' would become false and a lie, and that is disbelief. Similarly, everyone whom God calls misguided, it would be necessary to make his breast tight and constricted, and likewise everyone He finds misguided. Then God clarified the path for every disbeliever, and if he does not submit, He finds him misguided and calls him such, so it would be necessary to make his breast tight and constricted. Then every disbeliever, God expands his breast because He guided him and tightens his breast because He misguided him, and in that is a description of God of something impossible. Likewise, God's division of creation into two groups: one whose breast He expanded and the other whose breast He tightened is false. And all of this is disbelief.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation. The author first states the Maturidi position that God is the creator of all actions, including the acts of guidance and misguidance. Then he introduces a Quranic argument that demolishes the Mu'tazilite interpretations. The first verse is 'Innaka la tahdi man ahbabta' (Q28:56). If guidance (huda) were merely bayan (clarification), then the Prophet would have been able to guide his loved ones, but the verse denies that. Therefore, there must be a guidance beyond mere clarification, which is God's creation of the act of guidance in the servant. The second verse is 'Faman yuridillahu an yahdiyahu yashrah sadrahu lil-islam' (Q6:125). The author reasons that if the huda in this verse meant da'wa (calling) and bayan (clarifying the path), then everyone who receives that call would have an expanded breast, which contradicts the second part of the verse that some have tightened breasts. Since God clarifies the path for all disbelievers, yet they remain misguided, the logical conclusion is that every disbeliever would have an expanded breast for receiving guidance and a tightened breast for being misguided – a contradiction. This would make God's division of people into those with expanded and tightened breasts meaningless and false, which is tantamount to disbelief.

Key Terms
الهدى
البيان
الدعوة
شرح الصدر
ضيق الصدر
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Guidance (huda) is merely clarification (bayan) and does not require any creative act from God.
Correction: The Quranic verses show that there is a guidance beyond clarification, namely God's creation of the act of guidance in the servant. The Prophet could not guide even his beloved uncle, proving that true guidance comes only from Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the argument in this passage, if guidance (huda) were merely clarification (bayan), what would follow from Q28:56?
A) The Prophet would be able to guide whom he loved
B) The Prophet would not be able to guide anyone
C) Guidance would be impossible
D) God would guide everyone

Key Takeaway
Divine guidance is not merely clarifying the truth, but God's creation of faith in the heart, as proven by the Prophet's inability to guide even his loved ones.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God alone creates guidance, then your faith is not from your own intelligence or effort. Do you truly depend on Him to expand your chest, or do you rely on your own listening and learning? How will your prayer change tonight?
?
The Prophet could not guide his own uncle, even with all his love and argument. Who in your life have you been trying to convince by debate or pressure? Will you now turn to the only One who creates guidance and beg Him for their sake?
?
This passage teaches that disbelief is not ignorance but God constricting the heart. Does this not make you fear for those you love? How does this drive you to plead for His mercy more than to lecture?

Refuting Mu'tazilite Interpretations of Guidance
Refutation of Mu'tazilite interpretations of guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite interpretations that divine guidance is limited to the path to Paradise or is merely a label are invalid according to the Maturidi position.

Core Idea
God's will is absolute; guidance cannot be conditional or a mere label.

In this passage, the author tackles two Mu'tazilite attempts to limit God's guidance. Al-Jubba'i claimed that 'guidance' in the Quran refers only to showing the path to Paradise, while others said it is merely naming someone as guided. Using Quranic verses, the author demonstrates that God's will is sovereign and not constrained by human actions or labels, thus refuting both interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite view on guidance
Learn al-Jubba'i's interpretation that guidance (huda) is limited to guidance to the path of Paradise in the afterlife. The author rejects this by citing Quranic verses that show God guides whom He wills unconditionally.
This interpretation makes God's will dependent on human faith, which contradicts the verses.
2
Examine the Quranic refutation
Look at the verses cited: Q28:56, Q32:13, Q6:149, Q35:8. Notice how they emphasize God's absolute will in guiding or misguiding, not limited to Paradise or based on merit.
The author argues that if guidance were only to Paradise, then the verses about universal possibility would imply God is unjust or foolish, according to Mu'tazilite own principles.
3
Refute the naming claim
Understand the second Mu'tazilite claim that guidance/misguidance is mere labeling. The author argues that such labels cannot be attached to God's will; rather, misguidance is a created act (فعل الضلال) from God.
This refutes the idea that God's will is only about naming, preserving His active role in guidance and misguidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتأويل الجبائي أنه هداية طريق الجنة في الآخرة باطل، لأنه تعالى قال وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ والله لا يهدي طريق الجنة من شاء بل من مات على إيمانه، ثم عندهم لا يجوز أن لا يدخل الجنة من مات على إيمان ولم يرتكب الكبائر أو تاب عنها بعدما ارتكب ولو لم يدخل لصار ظالمًا ولا يجوز له أن يدخل الجنة من كفر وارتكب كبيرة، ومات قبل التوبة عنها فأي مشيئة في ذلك الله تعالى يدل عليه أنه تعالى قال: وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَا نَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَنهَا ولا يجوز صرفه إلى هداية طريق الجنة وقال تعالى: فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَنَكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ولا يهدي جميع الخلق إلى الجنة بل لو فعل ذلك لكان عندهم سفيها وقال تعالى : يُضِلُّ مَن يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ وهذا لا يتصور في هداية طريق الجنة، وبهذا يبطل قولهم : إنه أراد به التسمية أو وجوده ضالاً لأن ذلك مما لا يصح تعليقه بالمشيئة بل من وجد منه فعل الضلال
And al-Jubba'i's interpretation that it is guidance to the path of Paradise in the afterlife is false, because He Almighty said: 'But God guides whom He wills' (Q28:56). And God does not guide to the path of Paradise whomever He wills, but rather only those who die upon their faith. Then according to them, it is not permissible that he who dies upon faith and did not commit major sins or repented from them after committing them should not enter Paradise, and if he does not enter, He would become unjust, and it is not permissible for him to enter Paradise for one who disbelieved and committed a major sin and died before repenting from it. So what will is there in that? God Almighty indicates it by His saying: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance' (Q32:13). And it is not permissible to turn it to guidance to the path of Paradise. And He said: 'For if He had willed, He could have guided you all' (Q6:149). And He does not guide all creatures to Paradise; rather, if He did that, according to them He would be foolish. And He said: 'He misguides whom He wills and guides whom He wills' (Q35:8) And this cannot be conceived in guidance to the path of Paradise. And by this, their saying is invalidated that He intended by it naming or finding him misguided, because that is not something that can be attached to the will; rather, from whom the act of misguidance is found...
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage refutes two Mu'tazilite interpretations. First, al-Jubba'i's claim that huda in the verse refers to guidance to the path of Paradise in the afterlife. The author argues that this is false because God says 'yadī man yashā' (guides whom He wills), but guidance to Paradise is not based on mere will; it is based on dying in a state of faith. Furthermore, the Mu'tazilites themselves hold that the one who dies in faith must enter Paradise, and the one who dies in disbelief cannot, so there is no scope for God's will in that. Then the author cites verses showing that God's will is absolute: 'law shi'nā laātaynā kulla nafsin hudāhā' (if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance) and 'law shā'a lahadākum ajma'īn' (if He willed, He would guide you all). These indicate that God's guidance is universal in possibility, but He does not guide all to Paradise, because that would be 'safah' (folly) according to the Mu'tazilites, which is a contradiction. Second, the author refutes the claim that 'yudillu' means simply naming someone misguided or finding them misguided, because such actions cannot be attached to God's will. The act of misguidance (iḍlāl) is something created by God, not just a label. The argument is that if it were just naming, it would not be something that God wills; it would be a mere judgment. So the Mu'tazilite interpretation is invalid.

Key Terms
تأويل الجبائي
هداية طريق الجنة
المشيئة
التسمية
الوجود
فعل الضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That divine guidance is merely showing the way to Paradise and that misguidance is just a name or perception.
Correction: Guidance and misguidance are real acts of God's will, not limited to a path or a label. God's will is absolute and not constrained by human conditions.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject al-Jubba'i's interpretation that guidance refers to guidance to the path of Paradise?
A) Because Paradise is not mentioned in the verse
B) Because God's guidance to Paradise is not based on His will alone but on the person's faith
C) Because the Mu'tazilites deny Paradise
D) Because guidance is only in this world

Key Takeaway
God's will in guidance and misguidance is absolute and cannot be reduced to a mere path to Paradise or a label; it involves His creative act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly accept that God's guidance is entirely His will, or do you secretly believe you deserve it based on your actions?
?
When you read 'He misguides whom He wills', does your heart humbly submit, or do you find yourself trying to rationalize it away to feel more in control?
?
Is your faith in God's absolute will a source of peace that frees you from relying on your own deeds, or do you still cling to the illusion that you have a claim on His guidance?

Refuting 'Yudillu' as Naming
Refutes Mu'tazilite interpretation of 'yudillu' as naming or finding misguided.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite interpretation of 'yudillu' as naming or finding misguided is linguistically and theologically invalid.

Core Idea
The Arabic verb 'adalla' means to lead astray, not to name.

In this passage, the author refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that Allah's attribute of leading astray (idlaal) simply means calling someone misguided or finding them so. He first argues that such an interpretation cannot be attached to divine will, and then provides a crucial linguistic argument from the Arabic language itself.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Mu'tazilite claim
Start by understanding what the Mu'tazila are saying: that 'yudillu' means either naming someone misguided or finding them already misguided.
This interpretation avoids attributing actual misguidance to Allah.
2
Follow the first refutation
Read how the author argues that this meaning cannot be attached to will, because will concerns action. He compares it to saying Allah could call someone black or tall arbitrarily.
This shows the absurdity of detaching the verb from its causative meaning.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
Focus on the author's question: where in Arabic does 'adalla' mean to name? Learn the distinction between 'adalla' (to lead astray) and 'dallala' (to call misguided). The Quran uses 'adalla', so it cannot mean naming.
This is the key proof that refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا يبطل قولهم : إنه أراد به التسمية أو وجوده ضالاً، لأن ذلك مما لا يصح تعليقه بالمشيئة بل من وجد منه فعل الضلال يسمى ضالاً ضالاً، ويوجد ومن لم يوجد منه ذلك لا يسمى بذلك ولا يوجد كذلك والقول به كالقول بأن الله تعالى يسمى أسود من شاء ويجد طويلاً من شاء وهذا فاسد، فكذا ما نحن فيه. وما يبطل كلام المعتزلة أيضا أن نسألهم ما معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ فإن قالوا معنى ذلك أنه يسميهم ضالين ويحكم عليهم بالضلال قيل لهم: أليس أن الله قد خاطب العرب بلغتها فقال: بِلِسَانٍ عَرَب مُّبِينِ فلابد من نعم فيقال لهم: فإذا كان الله أنزل القرآن بلسان العرب فمن أين وجدتم في لغة العرب أن يقال أضل فلان فلانا أي سماه ضالا؟ فإن قالوا: وجدنا القائل يقول: إذا قال رجل لرجل ضال قد ضللته قيل لهم: قد وجدنا العرب يقولون: ضلل فلان فلاناً إذا سماه ضالاً، ولم نجدهم يقولون أضل فلان فلانا بهذا المعنى، فلما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ لم يجز أن يكون معنى ذلك الاسم والحكم إذ لم يجز في العرب أن يقال أضل فلان فلانا إذ سماه ضالاً
And by this their statement is refuted that He intended by it naming or finding him misguided, because that cannot be attached to will. Rather, whoever performs the act of misguidance is called misguided, misguided, and is found [so]. And whoever does not perform that is not called that and is not found so. To say that is like saying that Allah calls someone black if He wills and finds someone tall if He wills. This is corrupt. So too is what we are discussing. What also refutes the speech of the Mu'tazila is that we ask them: what is the meaning of His saying: 'And Allah leads astray the wrongdoers'? If they say: its meaning is that He names them misguided and judges them to be misguided, it is said to them: did not Allah address the Arabs in their language, saying: 'In a clear Arabic tongue'? So they must say yes. Then it is said to them: since Allah revealed the Quran in the language of the Arabs, where did you find in the Arabic language that one says 'adalla fulan fulanan' meaning 'he named him misguided'? If they say: we found a speaker saying: when a man says to a man 'misguided', 'I have named him misguided', it is said to them: we have found the Arabs saying: 'dallala fulan fulanan' if he named him misguided, and we have not found them saying 'adalla fulan fulanan' with this meaning. So when Allah said: 'And Allah leads astray the wrongdoers', it is not permissible that its meaning is that name and judgment, since it is not permissible in Arabic to say 'adalla fulan fulanan' when he named him misguided.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation that the verb 'yudillu' means simply calling someone misguided or finding them already misguided. The author argues that such an interpretation cannot be attached to will, because will concerns action. He compares it to saying Allah could call someone black or tall arbitrarily, which is absurd. He then presents a linguistic argument: the Quran is in Arabic, and the Arabs distinguish between 'dallala' (to call misguided) and 'adalla' (to lead astray). The verse uses 'adalla', so it cannot mean just naming. This refutes the Mu'tazilite reading.

Key Terms
إضلال
تسمية
الوجود ضالاً
لغة العرب
ضلل
أضل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verb 'yudillu' in the Quran means to name someone misguided or to find them misguided.
Correction: In Arabic, 'adalla' means to lead astray, while 'dallala' means to name misguided. The Quran uses 'adalla', so it cannot mean naming.

Checkpoint
What is the key linguistic distinction the author uses to refute the Mu'tazilite interpretation of 'yudillu'?
A) The verb 'أضل' is never used in the Quran
B) The Arabs use 'ضلل' for naming, not 'أضل'
C) The word 'ضلال' does not exist in Arabic
D) The Mu'tazila do not know Arabic

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite interpretation of 'yudillu' as naming fails because it contradicts the Arabic language, which distinguishes between 'adalla' (to lead astray) and 'dallala' (to call misguided).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'And Allah leads astray the wrongdoers', do you ever feel a secret relief that you are not among them? But what if your own hidden wrongdoings, the ones you have not repented from, place you in that category? How does knowing that 'yudillu' means Allah actually causes misguidance—not just labels—change the urgency of your repentance? Will you today examine your heart for any wrong that you have downplayed, and turn from it before the attribute becomes a reality for you?
?
The Mu'tazilites twisted a single verb to avoid a difficult truth. Are there any verses or attributes of Allah that you have reinterpreted to make them more comfortable for your own desires? What is stopping you from accepting Allah's words exactly as they are, even when they confront your pride or your sense of control? Ask yourself: am I willing to submit to the plain meaning, or am I like those who 'interpret' to escape?
?
This passage shows that the difference between two letters (أضل vs ضلل) changes the entire doctrine. Have you ever dismissed small linguistic details in the Quran as unimportant? How careful are you when reading the Quran—do you pay attention to every word, every form, as a matter of faith? Reflect on this: the next time you recite a verse, will you pause to consider its exact wording and its implications, knowing that a single verb form can be a matter of truth or falsehood?

The Forced Reinterpretation of Divine Will
Al-Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila on guidance and misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila's forced reinterpretation of 'will' as 'will of compulsion' reveals the weakness of their position, and how the universal nature of causes proves that guidance and misguidance are from Allah.

Core Idea
Forced reinterpretation is a sign of doctrinal weakness.

Al-Nasafi begins his refutation by pointing out that the Mu'tazila themselves felt compelled to reinterpret the divine will in the verses about guidance. This forced move shows that their original understanding was flawed. In this passage, he explains that the only reason they needed to do so is because they had already misinterpreted guidance itself. Then he argues that the causes and conditions for guidance and misguidance are universal, so attribution to Allah's will is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how al-Nasafi first states that the Mu'tazila's own actions confirm their falsehood.
Take note of the key terms: الهداية, الإضلال, المشيئة.
2
Understand the forced interpretation
Al-Nasafi says the Mu'tazila reinterpreted 'will' as 'will of compulsion'. Ask yourself why they needed to do this.
The answer: because they had already misinterpreted 'guidance' as something other than explanation of the religion.
3
Analyze the universal causes argument
The author explains that causes, conditions and states are common to all people. If guidance and misguidance were not from Allah's will, mentioning will would be meaningless.
This is the core logical argument.
4
See the conclusion
Al-Nasafi concludes that the verses affirm his position and refute the Mu'tazila. Reflect on how this argument fits into the larger debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يحقق بطلان ذلك أنهم عرفوا بطلانهم حتى صرفوا الهداية المذكورة في هذه الآيات إلى ما صرفنا نحن، وفسروا المشيئة بمشيئة الجبر، وإنما يحتاج إلى صرف المشيئة إلى مشيئة الجبر عند كون الهداية ما بينا دون بيان الدين بدلائله والتسمية والوجود وإراءه طريق الجنة فى الآخرة، ثم قد بينا إبطال مشيئة الجبر وبهذه الآيات بطل إضافته ذلك إلى الله تعالى لوجود السبب منه أو الشرط أو الحالة الحاملة على ذلك، لأن هذه المعاني عامة في حق الناس كافة، فلم تكن هداية من اهتدى عندهم بمشيئته ولا ضلال من ضل فلم يكن لتعليق ذلك بالمشيئة معنى، فصح أن الأمر كما بينا، وأن الآيات كلها ناطقة بصحة ما ذهبنا إليه وبطلان ما ذهبت إليه المعتزلة، والله الموفق. ولكون هذه المسألة عين مسألة خلق أفعال العباد لم نشتغل بتطويلها، وإيراد ما أورده سلف الأمة من الدلائل السمعية والعقلية. ولو تلقت المعتزلة ما نطق به كتاب الله تعالى من إضافة الهداية والإضلال إليه بالقبول، وتعلموا من أهل الحق دفع ما تتمسك به الثنوية من الشبهة، وهو أن الحكيم لا يفعل القبيح لكان خيراً لهم من أن تلقنوا من الثنوية هذه الشبهة، وتشبثوا بها، وجعلوها قانونا لكتاب الله فصرفوا ما لا يوافقها إلى وجوه مستكرهة وأولوه تأويلات غير منقادة، فحرفوا الكلم عن مواضعها، وأزالوا النصوص(۱) عن مواردها وراموا تسوية حكم الربوبية (۲) على ما خالوه عقلاً، وظنوه علمًا بالله من الخذلان وهو المستعان وعليه التكلان - والله الموفق (۳).
And among what confirms the falsehood of that is that they recognized their own falsehood to the extent that they diverted the guidance mentioned in these verses to what we diverted it, and they interpreted the will (al-mashī'a) as the will of compulsion (jabr). And there is need to divert the will to the will of compulsion only when the guidance is as we explained, not the explanation of the religion by its proofs, nor naming, nor existence, nor showing the way to Paradise in the hereafter. Then we have already demonstrated the nullification of the will of compulsion, and by these verses the attribution of that to Allah the Exalted is invalidated because of the existence of the cause from Him, or the condition, or the state that impels that. For these meanings are universal concerning all people. So with them, there is no guidance of one who is guided by His will, nor misguidance of one who goes astray; so there would be no meaning to attaching that to the will. So it is correct that the matter is as we explained, and that all the verses speak to the truth of what we hold and the falsehood of what the Mu'tazila hold. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And because this issue is exactly the issue of the creation of the acts of servants, we did not occupy ourselves with prolonging it and citing what the predecessors of the nation brought of transmitted and rational proofs. And if the Mu'tazila had accepted what the Book of Allah declares of the attribution of guidance and misguidance to Him, and had learned from the People of Truth to repel the doubt that the Dualists cling to — namely that the wise does not do evil — it would have been better for them than that they learn this doubt from the Dualists and cling to it, making it a canon for the Book of Allah, diverting what does not agree with it to objectionable interpretations and interpreting it with interpretations that are not straightforward, so they distorted words from their places and removed the texts from their contexts, and aimed to equate the judgment of Lordship with what they imagined rationally, and thought it knowledge of Allah, when it is from abandonment. And He is the one sought for help, and upon Him is reliance. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila interpretation of verses about divine guidance (hidāya) and misguidance (ḍalāl). The author begins by stating that what confirms the falsity of their position is that they themselves recognized the weakness of their view, as they felt compelled to reinterpret the word 'will' (mashī'a) in these verses as the 'will of compulsion' (mashī'at al-jabr). This is a forced interpretation: they twist the meaning to avoid attributing misguidance to God, but the only reason to do so is if one has already misinterpreted 'guidance' as something other than the explanation of the religion and its proofs. The author then reminds that the nullification of the 'will of compulsion' has already been established. The key point is that the causes, conditions, and impelling states for guidance and misguidance are universal to all people; they are common to both the guided and the misguided. Therefore, if guidance and misguidance were not attributed to God's will, there would be no rationale for mentioning will at all in these verses. The verses themselves, then, affirm the author's position and refute the Mu'tazila. The author then notes that this issue is essentially the same as the issue of the creation of acts, so he does not dwell on it further. Finally, he criticizes the Mu'tazila for taking their cue from the Dualists (al-thunawiyya) who claim that the wise does not do evil, rather than from the People of Truth. By adopting this as a principle, they distort the clear texts of the Qur'an and try to fit God's Lordship into their own rational categories, which is a form of abandonment (khidhlān). The passage ends with reliance on Allah.

Key Terms
الهداية
الإضلال
المشيئة
مشيئة الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila interpretation of 'will' in guidance verses is based on a sound linguistic analysis.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that their reinterpretation is forced and only arises because they had already misinterpreted the meaning of guidance itself.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what compelled the Mu'tazila to reinterpret the word 'will' (mashī'a) as 'will of compulsion'?
A) They had misinterpreted the meaning of guidance in the verses.
B) They wanted to affirm free will.
C) They were following the Ash'arite school.
D) They found a grammatical rule that required it.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's forced reinterpretation of divine will reveals the weakness of their position; the universal causes prove that guidance and misguidance are from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about guidance and misguidance, do you truly believe that your own guidance is entirely from Allah, or do you subtly feel that you earned it through your own effort? In light of al-Nasafi's argument, how can you deepen your reliance on Allah for hidayah?
?
Al-Nasafi accuses the Mu'tazila of 'recognizing their own falsehood' because they had to twist the meaning of the text. Is there any belief you hold that requires you to force or reinterpret clear scriptural texts? What would it take for you to honestly re-examine that position?
?
If divine will encompasses both guidance and misguidance, how does that affect the way you view people who are astray? Does it make you more compassionate or more resigned? How should it shape your du'a for them and your own fear of misguidance?

The Mu'tazila's Reliance on Dualist Principles
Al-Nasafi criticizes Mu'tazila for adopting Dualist principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi criticizes the Mu'tazila for borrowing the principle that 'the wise does not do evil' from the Dualists, and how this led them to distort the clear texts of the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Borrowing philosophical principles from Dualists leads to distortion of revelation.

In this concluding part of his refutation, al-Nasafi notes that the issue of guidance and misguidance is essentially the same as the creation of acts, so he does not elaborate further. Instead, he delivers a sharp critique: the Mu'tazila should have accepted the clear texts and learned from the People of Truth to rebut the Dualist doubt. Instead, they adopted that doubt as a principle and distorted the Qur'an to fit it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the connection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that al-Nasafi first connects this issue to the creation of acts.
He says this is the same issue, so no need to prolong.
2
Understand the Dualist doubt
Al-Nasafi mentions the Dualist doubt: 'the wise does not do evil'. Recognise that this is the principle the Mu'tazila adopted.
3
See the contrast: what should have been done
Al-Nasafi says the Mu'tazila should have accepted the texts and learned from the People of Truth to repel this doubt.
Instead, they learned the doubt from Dualists.
4
Note the consequences
The Mu'tazila made this principle a canon and distorted the clear texts. Reflect on how this led to misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And among what confirms the falsehood of that is that they recognized their own falsehood to the extent that they diverted the guidance mentioned in these verses to what we diverted it, and they interpreted the will (al-mashī'a) as the will of compulsion (jabr). And there is need to divert the will to the will of compulsion only when the guidance is as we explained, not the explanation of the religion by its proofs, nor naming, nor existence, nor showing the way to Paradise in the hereafter. Then we have already demonstrated the nullification of the will of compulsion, and by these verses the attribution of that to Allah the Exalted is invalidated because of the existence of the cause from Him, or the condition, or the state that impels that. For these meanings are universal concerning all people. So with them, there is no guidance of one who is guided by His will, nor misguidance of one who goes astray; so there would be no meaning to attaching that to the will. So it is correct that the matter is as we explained, and that all the verses speak to the truth of what we hold and the falsehood of what the Mu'tazila hold. And Allah is the Grantor of success. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself twisting a clear verse of the Qur'an because it didn't fit your sense of what Allah 'should' do? What will you do to prevent making your own reasoning a 'canon' for Allah's Book?
?
If you were to examine your heart, do you secretly hold any principle—like 'a wise being does not do evil'—that you place above Allah's own words? How can you reprioritize revelation over your own judgments?
?
Al-Nasafi says the Mu'tazila thought their rational imagination was 'knowledge of Allah' when it was actually 'abandonment.' Is there any belief you hold about Allah that you have not verified from the Qur'an and Sunnah? Will you commit today to seeking the truth from revelation alone?

The Doctrine of al-Aslah: God is Not Obliged to Create the Most Beneficial
Al-Nasafi states the Ahl al-Haqq position on al-aslah and refutes the Mu'tazila view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni (Ahl al-Haqq) position on al-aslah (the most beneficial) and how it refutes the Mu'tazila claim that God must always do the best for His servants.

Core Idea
God is not obligated to give the most beneficial; His grace is free, not a duty.

In this passage, al-Nasafi presents the core difference between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila regarding divine obligations. The Mu'tazila argue that God must create what is best for His servants, otherwise He would be unjust. Ahl al-Haqq respond that God's actions are not constrained by such human reasoning; He may do what He wills, and withholding benefit does not imply blame.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the two positions presented. Notice the structure: first the Ahl al-Haqq view, then the Mu'tazila view.
The passage uses technical terms like 'luṭf' (grace) and 'al-aṣlaḥ' (most beneficial).
2
Identify the key arguments of each group
Ahl al-Haqq argue that God can give a grace that would cause belief, but He is not obliged to do so; withholding it does not make Him blameworthy. The Mu'tazila argue that if God could give such grace and did not, He would be foolish and unjust.
Note the Mu'tazila conclusion: the utmost God can do is obligatory upon Him.
3
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider why this distinction matters for understanding divine justice and omnipotence. Ahl al-Haqq emphasize God's absolute freedom, while the Mu'tazila impose a moral framework on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤- الكلام في الأصلح: قال أهل الحق أن في مقدور الله تعالى لطفا لو فعل ذلك بالكفار لأمنوا اختيارا، ولم يفعل بهم ذلك ولم يكن بأن لم يعطهم ذلك بخيلاً ولا سفيها ولا جائراً ولا ظالما ، ولو فعل ذلك لكان منعمًا متفضلاً لا مؤديًا ما عليه، وإنه(٤) إذا لم بهم يعطهم ذلك فقد منعهم ما هو الأصلح لهم ، وكان إعطاؤه إياهم ذلك اللطف أصلح لهم من ترك الإعطاء، ويجوز أن يفعل بالعبد ما ليس بمصلحة له وإعطاء المصلحة) (٢) ليس بواجب على الله تعالى ولا إعطاء الأصلح، وليس لما في مقدور الله تعالى مما به الصلاح للعبد غاية ليس ورائها ما هو أصلح مما فعل. كلام المعتزلة في الأصلح]: وزعم جمهور المعتزلة أن ليس في مقدور الله تعالى لطف لو فعل بالكفار لأمنوا، ولو كان ذلك في مقدوره ولم يفعل ولم يعطهم ذلك لكان سفيها بخيلاً جائراً ظالمًا مانعا حقا مستحقاً، وغاية ما يقدر الله تعالى عليه مما به صلاح الخلق واجب
4. Discourse on al-aslah (the most beneficial): The People of Truth said: There is within the power of Allah the Exalted a grace (luṭf) such that if He did it to the disbelievers, they would believe voluntarily. And He did not do that to them, and He is not, by His not giving them that, stingy, nor foolish, nor unjust, nor oppressive. And if He did that, He would be benevolent and gracious, not one discharging an obligation upon Him. And when He does not give them that, He has prevented them from what is most beneficial for them, and giving them that grace would be more beneficial for them than withholding it. And it is permissible for Him to do to the servant what is not beneficial for him, and giving benefit is not obligatory upon Allah the Exalted, nor giving the most beneficial. And there is no limit to what is within the power of Allah the Exalted by which the servant's good is accomplished, beyond which there is something more beneficial than what He does. The speech of the Mu'tazila on al-aslah: The majority of the Mu'tazila claimed that there is not within the power of Allah the Exalted a grace such that if He did it to the disbelievers they would believe. And if that were within His power and He did not do it and did not give it to them, He would be foolish, stingy, unjust, oppressive, preventing a due right. And the utmost that Allah the Exalted is capable of by which the good of creation is accomplished is obligatory.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents the doctrine of al-aslah (the most beneficial) and contrasts the positions of Ahl al-Haqq (People of Truth, i.e., Ahl al-Sunna) and the Mu'tazila. The author, al-Nasafi, begins with the heading 'Discourse on al-aslah.' He first states the view of Ahl al-Haqq: God has the power to create a grace (luṭf) that, if applied to disbelievers, would cause them to believe voluntarily. However, God did not do this, and His not doing so does not make Him stingy, foolish, unjust, or oppressive. If He did it, it would be a favor (niʿma) and grace (tafaḍḍul), not the fulfillment of an obligation. The fact that He withholds it means He prevents them from what is most beneficial, yet He is not obligated to give it. It is permissible for God to do what is not beneficial for the servant, and neither benefit (maṣlaḥa) nor the most beneficial (al-aṣlaḥ) is obligatory upon Him. Moreover, there is no finite limit to what God can do for the servant's good such that beyond it there is something more beneficial. This refutes the idea that God must always do the best. Then al-Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila view: they deny that God has such a grace in His power because they argue that if He had it and did not use it, He would be foolish, stingy, unjust, etc. They also assert that the utmost God can do for the good of creation is obligatory (wājib) upon Him. This passage thus clearly delineates the Sunni position that God's actions are not constrained by human judgments of benefit or obligation, and that He does not incur blame for not doing what is most beneficial for creatures.

اللطف
المصلحة
الواجب

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ahl al-Sunna deny that God can do beneficial things.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna affirm that God can do beneficial things but is not obliged to do the most beneficial. Withholding benefit does not imply blame.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq, what is the ruling on God giving the most beneficial (al-aslah) to His servants?
A) It is obligatory upon God.
B) It is prohibited upon God.
C) It is not obligatory but permissible, and withholding it does not imply blame.
D) It is a due right of the servant.

Key Takeaway
God is not obliged to create the most beneficial for His servants; His actions are not bound by human notions of benefit or obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a trial or loss, do you ever accuse God in your heart of being unfair? How can this lesson reshape your understanding that God is not obliged to give you the best, yet He is not unjust when He withholds?
?
Do you view the blessings in your life as a right you deserve? This lesson teaches that God's grace is a favor, not a duty. How should this change your attitude of gratitude and submission?
?
Reflect on a specific moment when you thought God should have given you something better. How does the truth that giving the most beneficial is not obligatory upon God help you accept His decree and trust His wisdom?
